apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Pixies';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"pixies,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p>The
<b>Pixies</b>
are
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>
band
formed
in
<a
href="/wiki/Boston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston">Boston</a>,
Massachusetts,
in
1986.
The
group
currently
consists
of
founders
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Francis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Francis">Black
Francis</a>
(lead
vocals,
rhythm
guitar),
<a
href="/wiki/Joey_Santiago?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joey
Santiago">Joey
Santiago</a>
(lead
guitar)
and
<a
href="/wiki/David_Lovering?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Lovering">David
Lovering</a>
(drums).
Co-founder
<a
href="/wiki/Kim_Deal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kim
Deal">Kim
Deal</a>
(bass,
backing
vocals)
left
in
2013,
being
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Kim_Shattuck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kim
Shattuck">Kim
Shattuck</a>
as
a
live
bass
player
for
some
months;
in
December
she
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Paz_Lenchantin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paz
Lenchantin">Paz
Lenchantin</a>,
for
their
2014
world
tour.
The
Pixies
achieved
relatively
modest
commercial
success
in
their
home
country,
but
were
significantly
more
successful
in
the
United
Kingdom
and
mainland
Europe.
The
group
disbanded
in
1993
under
acrimonious
circumstances,
but
reunited
in
2004.</p>








<p>The
band's
style
of
music
contains
a
range
of
elements,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Indie_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Indie
rock">indie
rock</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Psychedelic_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psychedelic
rock">psychedelia</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Noise_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Noise
rock">noise
rock</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Surf_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surf
music">surf
rock</a>.
Black
Francis
is
the
Pixies'
primary
songwriter
and
singer.
He
has
written
about
a
number
of
offbeat
subjects
in
the
band's
songs,
such
as
extraterrestrials,
surrealism,
incest,
and
biblical
violence.</p>








<p>The
group
is
credited
as
having
significant
influence
on
the
alternative
rock
boom
of
the
1990s.
The
Pixies'
legacy
and
popularity
grew
in
the
years
following
their
break-up,
leading
to
sold-out
world
tours
following
their
reunion
in
2004.</p>








<p>In
June
2013,
bassist
Kim
Deal
officially
left
the
band,
and
shortly
after
the
band
released
a
new
track,
&quot;Bagboy&quot;—their
first
new
material
in
almost
ten
years.</p>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_.281986.29">Formation
(1986)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
(1986)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Joey
Santiago
and
Black
Francis
(born
Charles
Thompson
IV)
first
met
when
they
lived
next
to
each
other
in
a
suite
while
attending
the
<a
href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts_Amherst?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
of
Massachusetts
Amherst">University
of
Massachusetts
Amherst</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
Santiago
was
worried
about
distractions,
he
noticed
Francis
played
music
and
the
pair
began
to
jam
together.<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
Francis
then
embarked
on
a
student
exchange
trip
to
<a
href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Puerto
Rico">Puerto
Rico</a>
to
study
Spanish.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
six
months,
he
returned
to
Amherst
and
dropped
out
of
the
university.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Francis
and
Santiago
spent
1984
working
in
a
warehouse,
with
Francis
composing
songs
on
his
acoustic
guitar
and
writing
lyrics
on
the
subway
train.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
pair
formed
a
band
in
January
1986.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bass
player
Kim
Deal
joined
Santiago
and
Francis
two
weeks
later
after
responding
to
a
classified
advertisement
Francis
had
placed,
seeking
a
female
bass
player
who
liked
both
<a
href="/wiki/Folk_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Folk
music">folk
music</a>
icons
<a
href="/wiki/Peter,_Paul_and_Mary?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter,
Paul
and
Mary">Peter,
Paul
and
Mary</a>
and
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/H%C3%BCsker_D%C3%BC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;">H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Deal
was
the
only
person
to
respond,
but
arrived
at
the
audition
without
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bass_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bass
guitar">bass</a>
as
she
had
never
played
the
instrument
before.<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
was
invited
to
join
the
band
just
because
she
liked
the
songs
Black
Francis
was
showing
her.
She
later
obtained
a
bass,
and
the
trio
started
rehearsing
in
Deal's
apartment.<sup
id="cite_ref-Frank.2C_Ganz.2C_2005._p._20_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Frank.2C_Ganz.2C_2005._p._20-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
recruiting
Deal,
the
band
tried
unsuccessfully
to
get
her
sister,
<a
href="/wiki/Kelley_Deal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kelley
Deal">Kelley
Deal</a>,
to
join
as
its
drummer.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Kim's
husband
suggested
they
hire
drummer
David
Lovering,
whom
Kim
had
met
at
her
wedding
reception.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
arrived
at
a
name
after
Santiago
selected
the
word
&quot;pixies&quot;
randomly
from
a
dictionary
and
took
a
liking
to
how
it
looked
and
its
definition
as
&quot;mischievous
little
<a
href="/wiki/Elves?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elves"
class="mw-redirect">elves</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Once
the
band
had
settled
on
a
name
and
stable
line-up,
they
moved
rehearsals
to
Lovering's
parents'
garage
in
mid-1986.<sup
id="cite_ref-Frank.2C_Ganz.2C_2005._p._20_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Frank.2C_Ganz.2C_2005._p._20-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
began
to
play
shows
at
bars
in
and
around
the
Boston
area.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Record_contract_and_Come_On_Pilgrim_.281987.29">Record
contract
and
<i>Come
On
Pilgrim</i>
(1987)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Record
contract
and
Come
On
Pilgrim
(1987)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>While
the
Pixies
were
playing
a
concert
with
<a
href="/wiki/Throwing_Muses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Throwing
Muses">Throwing
Muses</a>,
they
were
noticed
by
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Gary_Smith_(record_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gary
Smith
(record
producer)">Gary
Smith</a>,
manager
of
<a
href="/wiki/Fort_Apache_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fort
Apache
Studios">Fort
Apache
Studios</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
told
the
band
he
&quot;could
not
sleep
until
you
guys
are
world
famous&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
produced
a
17-track
demo
at
Fort
Apache
soon
afterwards,
known
to
fans
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pixies_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pixies
(EP)">The
Purple
Tape</a>&quot;
because
of
the
tape
cover's
purple
background.
Funded
by
Francis'
father
at
the
cost
of
$1000,
the
recording
session
was
completed
in
three
days.<sup
id="cite_ref-Sisario.2C_2006._p._16_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Sisario.2C_2006._p._16-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Local
promoter
Ken
Goes
became
the
band's
manager,
and
he
passed
the
demo
to
<a
href="/wiki/Ivo_Watts-Russell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ivo
Watts-Russell">Ivo
Watts-Russell</a>
of
the
independent
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/4AD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="4AD">4AD</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Watts-Russell
nearly
passed
on
the
band,
finding
them
too
normal,
&quot;too
rock
'n'
roll&quot;,
but
signed
them
at
the
persuasion
of
his
girlfriend.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Upon
signing
with
4AD,
eight
tracks
from
the
Purple
Tape
were
selected
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Come_On_Pilgrim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Come
On
Pilgrim">Come
On
Pilgrim</a></i>
mini-LP,
the
band's
first
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
it,
Francis
drew
upon
his
experiences
in
Puerto
Rico,
mostly
in
the
songs
&quot;Vamos&quot;
and
&quot;Isla
de
Encanta&quot;;
the
album
included
lyrics
describing
the
poverty
in
Puerto
Rico.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
religious
lyrics
in
<i>Come
On
Pilgrim</i>
and
later
albums
came
from
his
parents'
<a
href="/wiki/Born-again_Christian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Born-again
Christian"
class="mw-redirect">born-again
Christian</a>
days
in
the
Pentecostal
Church.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Critic
Heather
Phares
sees
themes
such
as
sexual
frustration
(&quot;I've
Been
Tired&quot;)
and
incest
(&quot;Nimrod's
Son&quot;
and
&quot;The
Holiday
Song&quot;)
on
the
record.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"

Rosa</i>
and
<i>Doolittle</i>
(1988–1989)</span>

Rosa
and
Doolittle
(1988–1989)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

style="line-height:1.1em;"><span

<p><i>Come
On
Pilgrim</i>
was
followed
by
the
band's
first
full-length
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Surfer_Rosa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surfer
Rosa">Surfer
Rosa</a></i>.
The
album
was
recorded
by
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Albini?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Albini">Steve
Albini</a>
(who
was
hired
by
Watts-Russell
on
the
advice
of
a
4AD
colleague),<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
completed
in
two
weeks,
and
released
in
early
1988.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>
gained
the
Pixies
acclaim
in
Europe;
both
<i><a
href="/wiki/Melody_Maker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melody
Maker">Melody
Maker</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sounds_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sounds
(magazine)">Sounds</a></i>
gave
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>
their
&quot;Album
of
the
Year&quot;
award.
American
critical
response
was
also
positive
yet
more
muted,
a
reaction
that
persisted
for
much
of
the
band's
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
eventually
certified
Gold
in
the
U.S.
in
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
album
was
released,
the
band
arrived
in
England
to
support
Throwing
Muses
on
the
European
&quot;Sex
and
Death&quot;
tour—beginning
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mean_Fiddler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mean
Fiddler"
class="mw-redirect">Mean
Fiddler</a>
in
London.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
also
took
them
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Netherlands?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>,
where
the
Pixies
had
already
received
enough
media
attention
to
be
headlining
the
tour.
Francis
later
recalled:
&quot;The
first
place
I
made
it
with
the
Pixies
was
in
Holland.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
became
notable
for
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/In-joke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In-joke">in-jokes</a>,
such
as
playing
their
entire
<a
href="/wiki/Set_list?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Set
list">set
list</a>
in
alphabetical
order.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Meanwhile,
the
Pixies
signed
an
American
distribution
deal
with
major
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Elektra_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elektra
Records">Elektra</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Around
this
time,
the
Pixies
struck
up
a
relationship
with
the
British
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Gil_Norton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gil
Norton">Gil
Norton</a>.
Norton
produced
their
second
full
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Doolittle_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doolittle
(album)">Doolittle</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
was
recorded
in
the
last
six
weeks
of
1988
and
seen
as
a
departure
from
the
raw
sound
of
<i>Come
On
Pilgrim</i>
and
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>.
<i>Doolittle</i>
had
a
much
cleaner
sound,
largely
due
to
Norton
and
the
production
budget
of
<a
href="/wiki/United_States_dollar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States
dollar">US$</a>40,000,
which
was
quadruple
that
of
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Doolittle</i>
featured
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Here_Comes_Your_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Here
Comes
Your
Man">Here
Comes
Your
Man</a>&quot;,
which
biographers
Josh
Frank
and
Caryn
Ganz
describe
as
an
unusually
jaunty
and
pop-like
song
for
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monkey_Gone_to_Heaven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monkey
Gone
to
Heaven">Monkey
Gone
to
Heaven</a>&quot;
was
a
Top
10
<a
href="/wiki/Modern_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
rock">modern
rock</a>
radio
hit
in
the
U.S.,<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard_albums_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard_albums-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
reached
the
Top
100
in
the
U.K.<sup
id="cite_ref-uk_singles_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-uk_singles-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Like
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>,
<i>Doolittle</i>
was
acclaimed
by
fans
and
<a
href="/wiki/Music_critic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
critic"
class="mw-redirect">music
critics</a>
alike.<sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Hiatus_.281989.E2.80.931990.29">Hiatus
(1989–1990)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Hiatus
(1989–1990)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>After
<i>Doolittle</i>
tensions
between
Deal
and
Francis
came
to
a
head
(for
example,
Francis
threw
a
guitar
at
Deal
during
a
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Stuttgart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>),<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Deal
was
almost
fired
from
the
band
when
she
refused
to
play
at
a
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Frankfurt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-aston_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-aston-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Santiago,
in
an
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mojo
(magazine)">Mojo</a></i>,
described
Deal
as
being
&quot;headstrong
and
want[ing]
to
include
her
own
songs,
to
explore
her
own
world&quot;
on
the
band's
albums;
eventually
she
accepted
that
Francis
was
the
singer
and
had
musical
control
of
the
band,
but
after
the
Frankfurt
incident,
&quot;they
kinda
stopped
talking&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-aston_29-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-aston-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
became
increasingly
tired
during
the
post-<i>Doolittle</i>
&quot;Fuck
or
Fight&quot;
tour
of
the
United
States
and
fighting
among
members
continued.<sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
tour's
final
date
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York</a>,
the
band
was
too
exhausted
to
attend
the
end-of-tour
party
the
following
night
and
soon
announced
a
hiatus.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
this
time,
Santiago
and
Lovering
went
on
vacation,<sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
while
Francis
performed
a
short
solo
tour,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
made
up
of
a
number
of
concerts
to
generate
gas
money
as
he
traveled
across
the
country.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Deal
formed
a
new
band,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Breeders?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Breeders">The
Breeders</a>,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Tanya_Donelly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tanya
Donelly">Tanya
Donelly</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Throwing_Muses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Throwing
Muses">Throwing
Muses</a>
and
bass
player
<a
href="/wiki/Josephine_Wiggs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Josephine
Wiggs">Josephine
Wiggs</a>
of
Perfect
Disaster.<sup
id="cite_ref-breedersbiography_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-breedersbiography-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pod_(The_Breeders_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pod
(The
Breeders
album)">Pod</a></i>,
was
released
in
1990.<sup
id="cite_ref-breedersbiography_30-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-breedersbiography-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Bossanova.2C_Trompe_le_Monde.2C_and_break-up_.281990.E2.80.932002.29"><i>Bossanova</i>,
<i>Trompe
le
Monde</i>,
and
break-up
(1990–2002)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Bossanova,
Trompe
le
Monde,
and
break-up
(1990–2002)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

<p>In
1990,
all
members
of
the
group
except
for
Deal
moved
to
Los
Angeles.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lovering
stated
that
he,
Santiago,
and
Francis
moved
there
&quot;because
the
recording
studio
was
there&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
Unlike
previous
recordings,
the
band
had
little
time
to
practice
beforehand,
and
Black
Francis
wrote
much
of
the
album
in
the
studio.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Featuring
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Velouria?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Velouria">Velouria</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dig_for_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dig
for
Fire">Dig
for
Fire</a>&quot;,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bossanova?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bossanova">Bossanova</a></i>
reached
number
70
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard_albums_26-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard_albums-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
contrast,
the
album
peaked
at
number
three
in
the
United
Kingdom.<sup
id="cite_ref-uk_albums_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-uk_albums-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Also
in
1990,
the
Pixies
released
a
cover
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Butterfield?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Butterfield">Paul
Butterfield
Blues
Band's</a>
&quot;Born
in
Chicago&quot;
on
the
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A1iy%C3%A1t:_Elektra%27s_40th_Anniversary?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rub&aacute;iy&aacute;t:
Elektra's
40th
Anniversary">Rub&aacute;iy&aacute;t:
Elektra's
40th
Anniversary</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
continued
to
tour
and
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Trompe_le_Monde?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trompe
le
Monde">Trompe
le
Monde</a></i>
in
1991,
their
final
album
before
their
break-up.
The
album
included
&quot;U-Mass&quot;,
which
has
been
described
as
being
about
college
apathy,<sup
id="cite_ref-magnet_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-magnet-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
whose
guitar
riff
was
written
years
before
at
the
University
of
Massachusetts
before
Francis
and
Santiago
dropped
out.<sup
id="cite_ref-magnet_37-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-magnet-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
featured
a
cover
of
&quot;Head
On&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jesus_and_Mary_Chain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Jesus
and
Mary
Chain">The
Jesus
and
Mary
Chain</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
Also
that
year,
the
band
contributed
a
cover
of
&quot;I
Can't
Forget&quot;
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Leonard_Cohen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leonard
Cohen">Leonard
Cohen</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Tribute_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tribute
album">tribute
album</a>
<i><a
href="/wiki/I%27m_Your_Fan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'm
Your
Fan">I'm
Your
Fan</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
began
an
international
tour
on
which
they
played
stadiums
in
Europe
and
smaller
venues
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
then
embarked
on
an
uncomfortable
tour
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
on
their
<a
href="/wiki/Zoo_TV_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zoo
TV
Tour">Zoo
TV
Tour</a>
in
1992.<sup
id="cite_ref-barton_40-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barton-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Tensions
rose
between
band
members,
and,
at
the
end
of
the
year,
the
Pixies
went
on
sabbatical
and
focused
on
separate
projects.<sup
id="cite_ref-barton_40-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barton-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
early
1993,
Francis
announced
in
an
interview
to
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_(former)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Radio
5
(former)">BBC
Radio
5</a>
that
the
band
was
finished
and
offered
no
explanation
at
the
time,
unbeknownst
to
the
other
members
of
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
called
Santiago
and
subsequently
notified
Deal
and
Lovering
via
<a
href="/wiki/Fax?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fax">fax</a>,
in
January
1993.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
break-up,
the
four
members
embarked
on
separate
projects.
Black
Francis
renamed
himself
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Black?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Black"
class="mw-redirect">Frank
Black</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
he
released
several
solo
albums,
including
a
string
of
releases
with
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Black_and_the_Catholics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Black
and
the
Catholics"
class="mw-redirect">Frank
Black
and
the
Catholics</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-fbatcr_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-fbatcr-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
Deal
returned
to
The
Breeders,
who
scored
a
hit
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cannonball_(Breeders_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cannonball
(Breeders
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Cannonball</a>&quot;
from
that
group's
platinum-selling
<i><a
href="/wiki/Last_Splash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Splash">Last
Splash</a></i>
in
1993,
and
released
two
more
albums
several
years
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-breedersbiography_30-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-breedersbiography-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
formed
and
released
one
album
with
<a
href="/wiki/The_Amps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Amps">The
Amps</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Santiago
played
lead
guitar
on
multiple
Frank
Black
albums,<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
well
as
on
other
artists'
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
wrote
theme
music
for
the
show
<i><a
href="/wiki/Undeclared?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Undeclared">Undeclared</a></i>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fox
Broadcasting
Company">Fox</a>
television
and
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Crime_and_Punishment_in_Suburbia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crime
and
Punishment
in
Suburbia">Crime
and
Punishment
in
Suburbia</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-pharesmartinis_51-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pharesmartinis-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
formed
a
band
called
<a
href="/wiki/The_Martinis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Martinis">The
Martinis</a>
with
his
wife,
<a
href="/wiki/Linda_Mallari?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Linda
Mallari"
class="mw-redirect">Linda
Mallari</a>,
who
released
an
album
in
2004.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2004,
he
also
played
lead
guitar
on
the
album
&quot;Statecraft&quot;
by
the
novelist
and
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Charles_Douglas_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Charles
Douglas
(musician)"
class="mw-redirect">Charles
Douglas</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lovering
went
on
to
become
a
magician
and
made
occasional
appearances
as
&quot;The
Scientific
Phenomenalist&quot;,
performing
experiments
on
stage
and
occasionally
opening
for
Frank
Black
and
The
Breeders.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lovering
continued
to
do
some
drumming,
playing
with
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Cracker_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cracker
(band)">Cracker</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-pharesmartinis_51-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pharesmartinis-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
well
as
on
one
of
<a
href="/wiki/Tanya_Donelly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tanya
Donelly">Tanya
Donelly</a>'s
solo
albums,<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
on
the

song
&quot;Free&quot;,
which

on

<i><a
href="/wiki/Empire_Records?qsrc=3044"

title="Empire

soundtrack.<sup
id="cite_ref-pharesmartinis_51-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pharesmartinis-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>4AD
and
Elektra
Records
continued
to
release
Pixies
material
in

band's
absence.
They
released
the
best-of
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Death_to_the_Pixies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

to

Pixies">Death
to
the
Pixies</a></i>
(1997),<sup

href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
Peel-session
compilation
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pixies_at_the_BBC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pixies
at
the
BBC">Pixies
at
the
BBC</a></i>
(1998),<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
<i><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

'B'

'B'

compilation
(2001).<sup
id="cite_ref-b-sides_58-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-b-sides-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
Meanwhile,
in
2002
material
from
the
band's
original
17-track
demo
tape
was
released
as
an
EP,
<i><a

(EP)">Pixies</a></i>,
on
Cooking
Vinyl
in

id="cite_ref-59"

in

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup>

Black
has
also
used
these
labels
to
release
solo
work<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
albums
with
The
Catholics.<sup

The
Pixies
in

in











<a

<p>In
the
11
years
following
the
break-up,
rumors
sometimes
circulated
regarding
a
reunion.
Though
Frank
Black
steadfastly
dismissed
them,<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-magnet_37-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-magnet-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
he
did
begin
to
incorporate
an
increasing
number
of
Pixies
songs
in
his
sets
with
The
Catholics,<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
occasionally
included
Santiago
in
his
solo
work
and
Lovering's
magic
show
as
an
opening
act
to
concerts.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2003,
a
series
of
phone
calls
between
band
members
resulted
in
some
low-key
rehearsals,
and
soon
to
a
decision
to
reunite.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
February
2004,
a
full
tour
was
announced,<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
tickets
for
nearly
all
the
initial
tour
dates
sold
out
within
minutes.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
four-night
run
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Brixton_Academy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brixton
Academy">Brixton
Academy</a>
was
the
fastest
selling
in
the
venue's
20-year
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
Pixies
played
their
first
reunion
concert
on
April
13,
2004,
at
The
Fine
Line
Music
Cafe
in
<a
href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Minneapolis,
Minnesota"
class="mw-redirect">Minneapolis,
Minnesota</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
a
warm-up
tour
through
the
U.S.
and
Canada
was
followed
by
an
appearance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allbusiness_70-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allbusiness-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
then
spent
much
of
2004
touring
throughout
Brazil,
Europe,
Japan,
and
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-allbusiness_70-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allbusiness-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
won
the
Act-of-the-Year
award
in
the
2004
<i>Boston
Music
Awards</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
2004
reunion
tour
reportedly
grossed
over
$14&nbsp;million
in
ticket
sales.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
June
2004,
the
band
released
a
new
song,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bam_Thwok?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bam
Thwok">Bam
Thwok</a>&quot;
exclusively
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes_Music_Store?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes
Music
Store"
class="mw-redirect">iTunes
Music
Store</a>.
The
song
reached
number
one
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Official_Download_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Official
Download
Chart">UK
Official
Download
Chart</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
4AD
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wave_of_Mutilation:_Best_of_Pixies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wave
of
Mutilation:
Best
of
Pixies">Wave
of
Mutilation:
The
Best
of
Pixies</a></i>,
along
with
a
companion
DVD,
entitled
<i>Pixies</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
contributed
a
rendition
of
&quot;Ain't
That
Pretty
At
All&quot;
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Warren_Zevon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warren
Zevon">Warren
Zevon</a>
tribute
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Enjoy_Every_Sandwich:_Songs_of_Warren_Zevon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Enjoy
Every
Sandwich:
Songs
of
Warren
Zevon"
class="mw-redirect">Enjoy
Every
Sandwich</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bam_Thwok?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bam
Thwok">Bam
Thwok</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Ain't
That
Pretty
At
All&quot;
were
both
recorded
by
engineer
<a
href="/wiki/Ben_Mumphrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ben
Mumphrey">Ben
Mumphrey</a>,
the
former
at
<a
href="/wiki/Stagg_Street_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stagg
Street
Studios">Stagg
Street
Studios</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Van_Nuys,_CA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Van
Nuys,
CA"
class="mw-redirect">Van
Nuys,
CA</a>
and
the
latter
at
Metamorphosis
Studio
in
<a
href="/wiki/Vienna,_Austria?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vienna,
Austria"
class="mw-redirect">Vienna,
Austria</a>.</p>








<p>In
2005,
the
band
made
appearances
at
festivals
including
<a
href="/wiki/Lollapalooza?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;T
on
the
Fringe&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Newport_Folk_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Newport
Folk
Festival">Newport
Folk
Festival</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
continued
to
make
appearances
through
2006
and
2007,<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
culminating
in
their
first-ever
appearances
in
Australia.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
Since
2005,
Francis
has
at
various
times
stated
that
the
Pixies
recording
a
new
studio
album
was
either
a
possibility,<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
or
an
unlikelihood,<sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
main
obstacle
being
Deal's
reluctance
to
do
so.<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>To
celebrate
the
20th
anniversary
of
the
release
of
<i>Doolittle</i>,
the
Pixies
launched
a
tour
in
October
2009
where
they
performed
the
album
track-for-track,
including
the
associated
<a
href="/wiki/B-sides?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B-sides"
class="mw-redirect">B-sides</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-nmejune29_90-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nmejune29-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
began
in
Europe,<sup
id="cite_ref-nmejune29_90-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nmejune29-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
continued
in
the
United
States
in
November,<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
the
Australian
tour
following
in
March
2010,
then
New
Zealand,
and
more
European
dates
in
spring
2010,<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
back
to
North
America
in
fall
2010
and
into
spring
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
autumn
of
2011
the
&quot;Imaginary
Cities&quot;
tour
continued
the
&quot;Doolittle
Tour&quot;
as
they
played
many
venues
for
the
first
time.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Kim_Deal.27s_departure.2C_.22Bagboy.22_and_new_material_.282013.E2.80.93present.29">Kim
Deal's
departure,
&quot;Bagboy&quot;
and
new
material
(2013–present)</span>

<p>On
June
14,
2013,
it
was
announced
by
the
band's
Twitter
profile
that
Kim
Deal
had
left
the
band.
Deal
has
since
posted
new
solo
music
on
her
website
and
the
remaining
Pixies
have
welcomed
her
to
come
back
as
her
schedule
with
Breeders
allows.<sup
id="cite_ref-kdback_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-kdback-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
weeks
later,
the
band
released
a
new
song,
&quot;Bagboy&quot;,
as
a
free
download
via
the
Pixies
website.
The
song
features
Jeremy
Dubs
of
The
Bennies
and
formerly
of
Bunnies
on
vocals
in
place
of
Deal.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
July
1,
2013,
the
Pixies
announced
the
addition
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Muffs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Muffs">The
Muffs</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Pandoras?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Pandoras">The
Pandoras</a>
guitarist
and
vocalist
<a
href="/wiki/Kim_Shattuck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kim
Shattuck">Kim
Shattuck</a>,
who
would
be
replacing
Deal
for
the
band's
2013
European
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
also
have
new
music
in
the
works,
but
have
not
indicated
if
it
will
be
released
on
an
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
September
3,
2013
Pixies
released
a
new
EP
simply
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/EP1_(Pixies_EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="EP1
(Pixies
EP)">EP1</a></i>.
On
November
29,
2013,
Shattuck
announced
that
she
had
been
dismissed
from
the
band
that
day.<sup
id="cite_ref-shattuckleave_101-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-shattuckleave-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
2013,
<a
href="/wiki/Paz_Lenchantin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paz
Lenchantin">Paz
Lenchantin</a>
was
announced
as
the
new
bassist
for
the
2014
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
More
new
material
surfaced
when
Pixies
released
their
second
EP,
titled
<a
href="/wiki/EP2_(Pixies_EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="EP2
(Pixies
EP)">EP2</a>,
on
January
3,
2014.
The
single
released
to
radio
was
&quot;Blue
Eyed
Hexe.&quot;</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
Pixies'
musical
style
has
been
described
as
&quot;an
unorthodox
marriage
of
surf
music
and
punk
rock,
...
characterized
by
Black's
bristling
lyrics
and
hackle-raising
caterwaul,
Kim
Deal's
whispered
harmonies
and
waspy
basslines,
Joey
Santiago's
fragile
guitar,
and
the
persistent
flush
of
David
Lovering's
drums.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-barton_40-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barton-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
music
incorporates
extreme
dynamic
shifts;
Francis
explained
in
1991,
&quot;Those
are
the
two
basic
components
of
rock
music
[.
.
.]
the
dreamy
side
and
the
rockin'
side.
It's
always
been
either
sweaty
or
laid
back
and
cool.
We
do
try
to
be
dynamic,
but
it's
dumbo
dynamics,
because
we
don't
know
how
to
do
anything
else.
We
can
play
loud
or
quiet—that's
it&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guitar_Player_103-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guitar_Player-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Influences">Influences</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Influences">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
Pixies
draw
influence
from
a
range
of
artists
and
genres;
each
member
came
from
a
different
musical
background.
When
he
first
started
writing
songs
for
the
Pixies,
Francis
says
he
was
listening
to
nothing
but
<a
href="/wiki/H%C3%BCsker_D%C3%BC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;">H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Captain_Beefheart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Captain
Beefheart">Captain
Beefheart</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Iggy_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Iggy
Pop">Iggy
Pop</a>;<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
influences
associated
with
Francis
include
<a
href="/wiki/The_Gun_Club?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Gun
Club">The
Gun
Club</a><sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Cars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Cars">The
Cars</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
making
of
<i>Doolittle</i>
he
was
listening
heavily
to
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>'
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles
(album)">The
White
Album</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
has
cited
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Holly">Buddy
Holly</a>
as
a
model
for
his
compressed
songwriting.<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Santiago
listened
to
1970s
and
1980s
punk
including
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Flag
(band)">Black
Flag</a>,
as
well
as
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bowie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bowie">David
Bowie</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Guitarists
who
influenced
him
include
<a
href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimi
Hendrix">Jimi
Hendrix</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Les
Paul">Les
Paul</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Wes_Montgomery?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wes
Montgomery">Wes
Montgomery</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison">George
Harrison</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-110"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup>
Deal's
musical
background
was
folk
music
and
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country</a>;
she
had
formed
a
country-folk
band
with
her
sister
in
her
teenage
years,
and
played
covers
of
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Everly_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Everly
Brothers">The
Everly
Brothers</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hank_Williams?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hank
Williams">Hank
Williams</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-barton_40-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barton-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
artists
they
listened
to
included
<a
href="/wiki/XTC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="XTC">XTC</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gang
of
Four
(band)">Gang
of
Four</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Costello?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Costello">Elvis
Costello</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rogers_111-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rogers-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lovering
is
a
fan
of
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Rush_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rush
(band)">Rush</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-barton_40-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barton-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Other
media
such
as
film
has
had
an
impact
on
the
Pixies;
Francis
cites
surrealist
films
<i><a
href="/wiki/Eraserhead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eraserhead">Eraserhead</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Un_chien_andalou?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Un
chien
andalou"
class="mw-redirect">Un
chien
andalou</a></i>
(as
mentioned
in
&quot;Debaser&quot;)
as
influences.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialprofile_14-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialprofile-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
has
commented
on
these
influences,
saying
he
&quot;didn't
have
the
patience
to
sit
around
reading
Surrealist
novels&quot;,
but
found
it
easier
to
watch
twenty-minute
films.<sup
id="cite_ref-112"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Songwriting_and_vocals">Songwriting
and
vocals</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Songwriting
and
vocals">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Most
of
the
Pixies
songs
were
composed
and
sung
by
Francis.
Critic
Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine
has
described
Francis's
writing
as
containing
&quot;bizarre,
fragmented
lyrics
about
space,
religion,
sex,
mutilation,
and
pop
culture&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-bio_5-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-bio-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Biblical
violence
is
a
theme
of
<i>Doolittle</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;Dead&quot;
and
&quot;Gouge
Away&quot;;<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-113"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup>
Francis
told
a
<i>Melody
Maker</i>
interviewer,
&quot;It's
all
those
characters
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Old_Testament?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
Testament">Old
Testament</a>.
I'm
obsessed
with
them.
Why
it
comes
out
so
much
I
don't
know.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-114"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
has
described
<i>Come
on
Pilgrim<span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s</i>
&quot;Caribou&quot;
as
being
about
reincarnation,<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
extraterrestrial
themes
appear
in
a
number
of
songs
on
<i>Bossanova</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPIN_Life_Pixies_1-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPIN_Life_Pixies-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Deal
co-wrote
<i>Doolittle</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;Silver&quot;
with
Francis,<sup
id="cite_ref-doolittle_115-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-doolittle-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
they
share
lead
harmony
vocals
on
the
track.<sup
id="cite_ref-Sisario.2C_2006._p._16_15-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Sisario.2C_2006._p._16-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
co-wrote
and
sang
lead
vocals
on
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;Gigantic&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-surferrosa_116-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-surferrosa-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-117"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
is
the
sole
songwriter
of
the
2004
digital
single
&quot;Bam
Thwok&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-rogers_111-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rogers-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
was
credited
as
Mrs.
John
Murphy
on
the
former
composition<sup
id="cite_ref-surferrosa_116-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-surferrosa-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup>—at
the
time
she
was
married
and
she
used
this
name
as
an
ironic
<a
href="/wiki/Feminism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Feminism">feminist</a>
joke.<sup
id="cite_ref-119"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
sang
lead
vocals
on
the
song
&quot;Into
the
White&quot;
(which
is
another
song
she
and
Francis
co-wrote)
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Young?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neil
Young">Neil
Young</a>
cover
&quot;Winterlong&quot;,
both
B-sides.<sup
id="cite_ref-b-sides_58-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-b-sides-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lovering
sang
lead
vocals
on
<i>Doolittle</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;La
La
Love
You&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-doolittle_115-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-doolittle-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
B-side
&quot;Make
Believe&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-b-sides_58-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-b-sides-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Impact">Impact</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Impact">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Although
the
Pixies
produced
relatively
few
albums,
whose
sales
were
modest,
they
had
a
significant
influence
on
the
alternative
rock
boom
of
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstone_120-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstone-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-egan_121-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-egan-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
Gary
Smith,
who
produced
their
<i>Come
On
Pilgrim</i>,
commented
on
the
band's
influence
on
alternative
rock
and
their
legacy
in
1997:<sup
id="cite_ref-egan_121-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-egan-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<blockquote>









<p>I've
heard
it
said
about
<a
href="/wiki/The_Velvet_Underground?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Velvet
Underground">The
Velvet
Underground</a>
that
while
not
a
lot
of
people
bought
their
albums,
everyone
who
did
started
a
band.
I
think
this
is
largely
true
about
the
Pixies
as
well.
Charles'
secret
weapon
turned
out
to
be
not
so
secret
and,
sooner
or
later,
all
sorts
of
bands
were
exploiting
the
same
strategy
of
wide
dynamics.
It
became
a
kind
of
new
pop
formula
and,
within
a
short
while,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit">Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit</a>&quot;
was
charging
up
the
charts
and
even
the
members
of
Nirvana
said
later
that
it
sounded
for
all
the
world
like
a
Pixies
song.</p>








</blockquote>








<p>Sonically,
the
Pixies
are
credited
with
popularizing
the
extreme
dynamics
and
stop-start
timing
that
would
become
widespread
in
alternative
rock;
Pixies
songs
typically
feature
hushed,
restrained
verses,
and
explosive,
wailing
choruses.<sup
id="cite_ref-magnet_37-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-magnet-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Artists
including
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bowie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bowie">David
Bowie</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/PJ_Harvey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PJ
Harvey">PJ
Harvey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Strokes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Strokes">The
Strokes</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Weezer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Weezer">Weezer</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Pavement_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pavement
(band)">Pavement</a>
have
cited
admiration
of
or
influence
by
the
Pixies.<sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-carew_23-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-carew-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-rhino_122-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rhino-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_123-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Bono?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bono">Bono</a>
of
U2
has
called
the
Pixies
&quot;one
of
America's
greatest
bands
ever&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-rhino_122-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rhino-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-124"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Radiohead's
<a
href="/wiki/Thom_Yorke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thom
Yorke">Thom
Yorke</a>
has
said
that,
while
at
school,
&quot;the
Pixies
had
changed
my
life&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-egan_121-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-egan-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bowie,
whose
own
music
had
inspired
Francis
and
Santiago
while
they
were
at
university,
has
said
that
the
Pixies
made
&quot;just
about
the
most
compelling
music
of
the
entire
80s.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rhino_122-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rhino-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>One
notable
citation
as
an
influence
was
by
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>,
on
influencing
Nirvana's
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;,
which
he
admitted
was
a
conscious
attempt
to
co-opt
the
Pixies'
style.
In
a
January
1994
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>,
he
said,
&quot;I
was
trying
to
write
the
ultimate
pop
song.
I
was
basically
trying
to
rip
off
the
Pixies.
I
have
to
admit
it
[smiles].
When
I
heard
the
Pixies
for
the
first
time,
I
connected
with
that
band
so
heavily
I
should
have
been
in
that
band—or
at
least
in
a
Pixies
cover
band.
We
used
their
sense
of
dynamics,
being
soft
and
quiet
and
then
loud
and
hard.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-egan_121-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-egan-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-125"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
cited
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>
as
one
of
his
main
musical
influences,
and
particularly
admired
the
album's
natural
and
powerful
drum
sounds—a
result
of
Steve
Albini's
influence
on
the
record.
Albini
later
produced
Nirvana's
1993
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Utero_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Utero
(album)">In
Utero</a></i>
at
the
request
of
Cobain.<sup
id="cite_ref-126"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_videos_and_DVDs">Music
videos
and
DVDs</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Pixies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Music
videos
and
DVDs">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>No
music
videos
were
released
from
<i>Come
on
Pilgrim</i>
or
<i>Surfer
Rosa</i>,
but
from
<i>Doolittle</i>
onwards,
the
following
videos
were
made:
&quot;Monkey
Gone
To
Heaven&quot;,
&quot;Here
Comes
Your
Man&quot;,
&quot;Velouria&quot;,
&quot;Dig
For
Fire&quot;,
&quot;Allison&quot;,
&quot;Alec
Eiffel&quot;,
&quot;Head
On&quot;,
and
&quot;Debaser&quot;;<sup
id="cite_ref-jawetz_127-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jawetz-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
these
were
later
released
on
the
2004
DVD
<i>Pixies</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-jawetz_127-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jawetz-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
Furthermore,
a
music
video
accompanied
the
release
of
their
2013
song,
&quot;Bagboy&quot;,
as
well
an
alternate
video
released
on
a
later
date.
Videos
have
been
made
for
all
the
songs
in
EP1.
The
videos
for
&quot;Here
Comes
Your
Man&quot;
and
&quot;Allison&quot;
were
also
released
on
<i>The
Complete
'B'
Sides</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-b-sides_58-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-b-sides-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>By
<i>Bossanova</i>,
the
band
had
developed
a
severe
aversion
to
recording
music
videos,
and
Francis
refused
to
<a
href="/wiki/Lip-sync?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lip-sync"
class="mw-redirect">lip-sync</a>
to
them.<sup
id="cite_ref-pg140_128-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pg140-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
example,
in
the
&quot;Here
Comes
Your
Man&quot;
video,
both
Black
and
Deal
open
their
mouths
wide
instead
of
mouthing
their
lyrics.<sup
id="cite_ref-129"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
the
record
label
this
became
one
of
the
reasons
that
the
Pixies
never
achieved
major
coverage
on
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-pg140_128-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pg140-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>With
<i>Bossanova</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
release,
4AD
hoped
to
get
the
Pixies
chosen
to
perform
their
single
&quot;Velouria&quot;
on
the
BBC
music
program
<i><a
href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
of
the
Pops">Top
of
the
Pops</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-130"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup>
To
this
end,
the
band
was
pressured
into
producing
a
video
for
the
song,
and
they
made
one
cheaply
with
the
band
members
filmed
running
down
a
quarry,
shown
in
slow
motion.<sup
id="cite_ref-pg140_128-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pg140-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-barding_131-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barding-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
was
ultimately
not
given
a
spot
on
the
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-barding_131-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barding-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-132"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
90-minute
documentary
called
<i>loudQUIETloud:
a
film
about
the
Pixies</i>
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Cantor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Cantor">Steven
Cantor</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Matthew_Galkin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matthew
Galkin">Matthew
Galkin</a>
was
released
in
2006.
The
film
documents
their
2004
reunion
and
tour,
and
covers
the
years
after
the
break-up.<sup
id="cite_ref-133"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition
to
<i>Pixies</i>
and
<i>LoudQUIETloud</i>,
four
other
Pixies'
DVDs
were
released
between
2004
and
2006,
all
featuring
concert
performances:
<i>Live
at
the
Town
and
Country
Club
1988</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-134"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>The
Pixies—Sell
Out</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-rhino_122-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rhino-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>The
Pixies
Acoustic:
Live
in
Newport</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-135"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<i>The
Pixies
Club
Date:
Live
at
the
Paradise
in
Boston</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-136"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Pixies&page=1&ac=24&qid=2EA3787416CFD61651B72100B21556D3&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
